    523  3554							;----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    524  3554							; handle pause button for 2600 and 7800
    525  3554
    526  3554							; Timings:  NOT including palette setting or platform detect
    527  3554							; 2600:     no button press:	 11 cycles
    528  3554							;	     with button press:  21 cycles
    529  3554							; 7800      no button press:	 16 cycles
    530  3554							;	     with button press:  21 cycles
    531  3554
    532  3554
    533  3554
    534  3554		       00 08	   BW_SWITCH  =	$08	; NOTE: Shares bit position with SWCHB COLOUR/B&W SWITCH
    535  3554
    536  3554		       24 80		      bit	gameMode
    537  3556		       50 0b		      bvc	.pause7800	; 7800 platform
    538  3558
    539  3558							; 2600 pause logic...
    540  3558
    541  3558		       ad 82 02 	      lda	SWCHB
    542  355b		       45 80		      eor	gameMode
    543  355d		       29 08		      and	#BW_SWITCH
    544  355f		       f0 17		      beq	.setPauseCol	; no different to original state = no pause change
    545  3561		       d0 0f		      bne	.buttonDown	; unconditional
    546  3563
    547  3563							; 7800 pause logic...
    548  3563
    549  3563							; When the button is pressed, we check if it's the FIRST time it's pressed.
    550  3563							; This FIRST time is indicated by the PFLAG7800 being clear.  If it's the first time, we toggle the pause
    551  3563							; flag (BIT6) AND we toggle the PFLAG7800 so continued button-down does nothing.  When the button is
    552  3563							; released, then we again toggle the PFLAG7800, allowing a FIRST time check once again, when the button
    553  3563							; is next pressed.
    554  3563
    555  3563		       a9 08	   .pause7800 lda	#BW_SWITCH
    556  3565		       2c 82 02 	      bit	SWCHB
    557  3568		       f0 04		      beq	.pausePress
    558  356a		       05 80		      ora	gameMode	; not pressed, so enable first time press
    559  356c		       d0 08		      bne	.fixPause	; unconditional
    560  356e
    561  356e		       24 80	   .pausePress bit	gameMode
    562  3570		       f0 06		      beq	.setPauseCol	; NOT the first time in pause - so do nothing new
    563  3572
    564  3572							; Button is down, and we have detected it as a FIRST-TIME button press.
    565  3572
    566  3572		       45 80	   .buttonDown eor	gameMode	; toggle first time flag(7800) or current switch state(2600)
    567  3574		       49 80		      eor	#GAMEMODE_PAUSED	; toggle pause flag
    568  3576		       85 80	   .fixPause  sta	gameMode
    569  3578
    570  3578		       a5 80	   .setPauseCol lda	gameMode	; are we paused?
    571  357a		       10 07		      bpl	.exitPause	; only show pause colour when actually paused
    572  357c
    573  357c		       a6 81		      ldx	Platform
    574  357e		       bd e9 f5 	      lda	pscol,x
    575  3581		       85 aa		      sta	BGColour	; set main screen background colour.  RED is paused.
    576  3583
    577  3583				   .exitPause

    598  3591
    599  3591							; Handle the player joystick reading. We do it *every frame* so that we can incorporate a two-frame
    600  3591							; buffer.  This is designed to give a little better responsiveness to the 'quick tap' movement.
    601  3591
    602  3591		       a5 90		      lda	BufferedJoystick	; previous frame
    603  3593		       85 91		      sta	BufferedJoystick+1	; -> buffered
    604  3595
    605  3595							; Create a 'standardised' joystick with D4-D7 having bits CLEAR if the appropriate direction is chosen.
    606  3595							; P2 is shifted UP, so we don't need to worry in usage elsewhere (it's same format as a P1 joystick)
    607  3595
    608  3595		       a5 99		      lda	whichPlayer	; 3
    609  3597		       25 a7		      and	jtoggle	; 3
    610  3599		       aa		      tax		; 2
    611  359a

    613  359c		       85 92		      sta	BufferedButton	; 3 = 15
    614  359e

    616  35a1

    618  35a2		       30 04		      bmi	notP2	; 2/3= 8/9
    619  35a4
    620  35a4		       0a		      asl		; 2
    621  35a5		       0a		      asl		; 2
    622  35a6		       0a		      asl		; 2
    623  35a7		       0a		      asl		; 2 =	8
    624  35a8		       85 90	   notP2      sta	BufferedJoystick	; 3
    625  35aa
    626  35aa
    627  35aa							; "Scoring timer" reset stomp comment
    628  35aa
    629  35aa		       a5 c2		      lda	scoringTimer
    630  35ac		       f0 0a		      beq	timer0now
    631  35ae		       c6 c2		      dec	scoringTimer
    632  35b0		       d0 06		      bne	timer0now
    633  35b2		       a5 c3		      lda	scoringFlags
    634  35b4		       29 fc		      and	#<(~DISPLAY_FLAGS)	;	 switches to time display
    635  35b6		       85 c3		      sta	scoringFlags
    636  35b8				   timer0now
    637  35b8
    638  35b8							; fall through
    639  35b8
    640  35b8							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    641  35b8							; Player animation happens *every* frame so that we get good animation speeds.  Note that
    642  35b8							; the player animation consists of running a small animation 'program', and then actually drawing
    643  35b8							; the player.	The draw is the neat bit, because all it does is update some self-modifying pointers
    644  35b8							; inside the actual draw kernel in the appropriate bank.
    645  35b8
    646  35b8
      0  35b8					      DEFINE_SUBROUTINE	AnimatePlayers	; in GENERIC_BANK_1
      1  35b8		       00 06	   BANK_AnimatePlayers =	_CURRENT_BANK
      2  35b8					      SUBROUTINE
      3  35b8				   AnimatePlayers
    648  35b8
    649  35b8							; Optimised 7/1/2012 -- single page tables
    650  35b8
    651  35b8							; This interesting code performs the animations for the player(s) and sets the
    652  35b8							; pointers INSIDE the row bank for the draw code to point to the correct player
    653  35b8							; shape.  Kind of neat, as it doesn't require any shape copying (=speed!)
    654  35b8
    655  35b8
    656  35b8							; Cycle the player through his animation list.  The animation of a player is a direct
    657  35b8							; pointer to the actual shape used to display the player.  This shape is in turn
    658  35b8							; written to the current bank's self-modifying locations for the draw.  Since
    659  35b8							; we are effectively drawing from this current bank, the same code can be used
    660  35b8							; to 'undraw' the player as required.
    661  35b8
    662  35b8
    663  35b8							; x = player index
    664  35b8							; sets ManAnimation = FRAME to display for player
    665  35b8							; ManAnimation = index of player program into Manimate list
    666  35b8
    667  35b8		       24 80		      bit	gameMode
    668  35ba		       30 2c		      bmi	AnimationOK	; don't animate during pause
    669  35bc
    670  35bc		       c6 9f		      dec	ManDelayCount
    671  35be		       10 28		      bpl	AnimationOK
    672  35c0
    673  35c0		       a4 a0	   ReloadAnimation ldy	ManAnimation
    674  35c2		       b9 00 f7    ContinueAnim lda	Manimate,y	; delay count
    675  35c5		       d0 07		      bne	NewFrameOK
    676  35c7		       b9 01 f7 	      lda	Manimate+1,y
    677  35ca		       a8		      tay
    678  35cb		       4c c2 f5 	      jmp	ContinueAnim
    679  35ce
    680  35ce		       10 0d	   NewFrameOK bpl	doDelay
    681  35d0
    682  35d0		       c8		      iny		; handle a REFLECT
    683  35d1		       a5 a3		      lda	ManLastDirection
    684  35d3		       29 f7		      and	#%11110111
    685  35d5		       19 00 f7 	      ora	Manimate,y
    686  35d8		       85 a3		      sta	ManLastDirection
    687  35da
    688  35da		       c8		      iny
    689  35db		       d0 e5		      bne	ContinueAnim
    690  35dd
    691  35dd		       85 9f	   doDelay    sta	ManDelayCount
    692  35df
    693  35df		       c8		      iny
    694  35e0		       b9 00 f7 	      lda	Manimate,y
    695  35e3		       85 a2		      sta	ManAnimationFrameLO
    696  35e5
    697  35e5		       c8		      iny
    698  35e6		       84 a0		      sty	ManAnimation
    699  35e8
    700  35e8		       60	   AnimationOK rts
    701  35e9
    702  35e9
    703  35e9
    704  35e9		       40 40	   pscol      .byte.b	$40, $40
    705  35eb		       60 60		      .byte.b	$60, $60
    706  35ed
    707  35ed							;------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    708  35ed
------- FILE i2c_v2.2.inc LEVEL 3 PASS 3
      0  35ed					      include	"i2c_v2.2.inc"
      1  35ed							;
      2  35ed							; i2c_v2.2.inc
      3  35ed							;
      4  35ed							;
      5  35ed							; AtariVox EEPROM Driver
      6  35ed							;
      7  35ed							; By Alex Herbert, 2004
      8  35ed							;
      9  35ed							; Optimisations by Thomas Jentzsch, 2006/2008
     10  35ed							;
     11  35ed
     12  35ed
     13  35ed							; I/O Constants
     14  35ed
     15  35ed		       00 04	   I2C_SDA_MASK equ	$04
     16  35ed		       00 08	   I2C_SCL_MASK equ	$08
     17  35ed
     18  35ed
     19  35ed							; Signalling Macros
     20  35ed
     21  35ed							;  MAC     I2C_SCL_0
     22  35ed							;    lda     #$00
     23  35ed							;    sta     SWCHA
     24  35ed							;  ENDM
     25  35ed
     26  35ed							;  MAC     I2C_SCL_1
     27  35ed							;    lda     #I2C_SCL_MASK
     28  35ed							;    sta     SWCHA
     29  35ed							;  ENDM
     30  35ed
     31  35ed							;  MAC     I2C_SDA_IN
     32  35ed							;    lda     #I2C_SCL_MASK
     33  35ed							;    sta     SWACNT
     34  35ed							;  ENDM
     35  35ed
     36  35ed							;  MAC     I2C_SDA_OUT
     37  35ed							;    lda     #I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK
     38  35ed							;    sta     SWACNT
     39  35ed							;  ENDM
     40  35ed
     41  35ed
     42  35ed					      MAC	i2c_start
     43  35ed							; I2C_SCL_1
     44  35ed					      lda	#(I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK)*2	; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK
     45  35ed					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
     46  35ed							; I2C_SDA_OUT
     47  35ed					      lsr		; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK
     48  35ed					      sta	SWACNT	; 4
     49  35ed							; total: 12 cycles
     50  35ed					      ENDM
     51  35ed
     52  35ed
     53  35ed					      MAC	i2c_txbit
     54  35ed							; I2C_SCL_0
     55  35ed					      lda	#%0011	; 2
     56  35ed					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
     57  35ed							; set bit
     58  35ed					      adc	#%1000	; 2
     59  35ed					      sta	SWACNT	; 4	     SDA = !C (a = %1000 / %1100)
     60  35ed							; I2C_SCL_1
     61  35ed					      lda	#I2C_SCL_MASK	; 2
     62  35ed					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
     63  35ed							; total: 18 cycles
     64  35ed					      ENDM
     65  35ed
     66  35ed
     67  35ed					      MAC	i2c_txnack
     68  35ed							; I2C_SCL_0
     69  35ed					      lda	#I2C_SCL_MASK*2	; 2	     $00
     70  35ed					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
     71  35ed							; I2C_SDA_IN
     72  35ed					      lsr		; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK
     73  35ed					      sta	SWACNT	; 4
     74  35ed							; I2C_SCL_1
     75  35ed					      nop		; 2	     required for timing!
     76  35ed					      sta	SWCHA	; 4	     I2C_SCL_MASK
     77  35ed							; total: 18 cycles
     78  35ed					      ENDM
     79  35ed
     80  35ed
     81  35ed							; Subroutine Macros
     82  35ed
     83  35ed					      MAC	i2c_subs
     84  35ed
     85  35ed				   i2c_startread
     86  35ed							; use V to flag if previous byte needs ACK
     87  35ed					      ldy	#%10100001	; 2	     eeprom read command
     88  35ed					      .byte	$2c	; 2
     89  35ed				   i2c_startwrite
     90  35ed					      ldy	#%10100000	; 2	     eeprom write command
     91  35ed					      I2C_START		;12	     start signal (clears V flag)
     92  35ed					      tya		; 2 = 16
     93  35ed				   i2c_txbyte
     94  35ed					      eor	#$ff	; 2	     invert data byte
     95  35ed					      sec		; 2
     96  35ed					      rol		; 2 =	6    shift loop bit into a
     97  35ed				   i2c_txbyteloop
     98  35ed					      tay		; 2
     99  35ed					      I2C_TXBIT		;18	     transmit
    100  35ed					      tya		; 2
    101  35ed					      asl		; 2	     shift next bit into C
    102  35ed					      bne	i2c_txbyteloop	; 2= 26/27
    103  35ed
    104  35ed							; receive acknowledge bit
    105  35ed
    106  35ed					      beq	i2c_rxbit	;43 = 43
    107  35ed							; i2c_txbyte: 264 cycles
    108  35ed							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    109  35ed
    110  35ed				   i2c_rxbyte
    111  35ed					      bvc	i2c_rxskipack	; 2	     previous byte needs acknowledge?
    112  35ed					      jsr	i2c_txack	;24	     transmit acknowledge bit
    113  35ed
    114  35ed				   i2c_rxskipack
    115  35ed					      bit	i2c_rxbyte	; 4	     set V - next byte(s) require acknowledge
    116  35ed
    117  35ed					      lda	#1	; 2
    118  35ed				   i2c_rxbyteloop
    119  35ed					      tay		; 2 =	2
    120  35ed				   i2c_rxbit		;	     receive bit in C
    121  35ed					      I2C_TXNACK		;18 = 18
    122  35ed
    123  35ed					      lda	SWCHA	; 4
    124  35ed					      lsr		; 2
    125  35ed					      lsr		; 2
    126  35ed					      lsr		; 2 = 10    C = SDA
    127  35ed
    128  35ed					      tya		; 2
    129  35ed					      rol		; 2	     rotate into Y
    130  35ed					      bcc	i2c_rxbyteloop	; 2=	6/7
    131  35ed
    132  35ed							; received byte in A
    133  35ed					      rts		; 6 =	6
    134  35ed							; i2c_rxbit:  40 cycles
    135  35ed							; i2c_rxbyte: 310/333 cycles
    136  35ed							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    137  35ed
    138  35ed				   i2c_stopread
    139  35ed					      bvc	i2c_stopwrite	; 2
    140  35ed					      ldy	#$80	; 2
    141  35ed					      jsr	i2c_rxbit	;46	     transmit no-acknowledge
    142  35ed
    143  35ed				   i2c_stopwrite
    144  35ed					      jsr	i2c_txack	;30
    145  35ed
    146  35ed							; return port to input mode
    147  35ed					      lda	#0	; 2	     0
    148  35ed					      sta	SWACNT	; 4
    149  35ed					      rts		; 6 = 12
    150  35ed							; i2c_stopread:  45/92
    151  35ed							; i2c_stopwrite: 42
    152  35ed							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    153  35ed
    154  35ed				   i2c_txack
    155  35ed							; I2C_SCL_0
    156  35ed					      lda	#0	; 2	     $00
    157  35ed					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
    158  35ed							; I2C_SDA_OUT
    159  35ed					      lda	#(I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK)	; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK
    160  35ed					      sta	SWACNT	; 4
    161  35ed							; I2C_SCL_1
    162  35ed					      asl		; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK
    163  35ed					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
    164  35ed
    165  35ed					      rts		; 6
    166  35ed							; total: 24 cycles
    167  35ed							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    168  35ed
    169  35ed					      ENDM
    170  35ed
    171  35ed
    172  35ed

    741  3658
    742  3658							; assume no SaveKey found:
    743  3658		       a9 ff		      lda	#$ff	; 2	     return $ff if no SaveKey found
    744  365a		       85 de		      sta	highScoreSK+2	; 3

    747  365c		       a5 df		      lda	startCave	; 3	     load start cave*5 and level
    748  365e		       a6 ac		      ldx	level	; 3

    750  3663		       90 52		      bcc	NoSKfound	; 2/3

    761  366d				   .loopRead

    763  3670		       c9 ff		      cmp	#$ff	; 2	     EEPROM slot empty?
    764  3672		       d0 02		      bne	.skipEmpty	; 2/3	      no, skip clear
    765  3674		       a9 00		      lda	#0	; 2	     clear EEPROM slot

      0  3699					      DEFINE_SUBROUTINE	SetupSaveKey	; = 853
      1  3699		       00 06	   BANK_SetupSaveKey =	_CURRENT_BANK
      2  3699					      SUBROUTINE
      3  3699				   SetupSaveKey
    805  3699
    806  3699							; calculate slot;
    807  3699							; a = cave (5*n): A=$00; E=$05; I=$0a; M=$0f
    808  3699							; x = level (0..4)
    809  3699		       85 e1		      sta	offsetSK	; 3
    810  369b		       8a		      txa		; 2
    811  369c		       18		      clc		; 2

      0  3845					      DEFINE_SUBROUTINE	CopyROMShadowToRAM	; in INITBANK
      1  3845		       00 07	   BANK_CopyROMShadowToRAM =	_CURRENT_BANK
      2  3845					      SUBROUTINE
      3  3845				   CopyROMShadowToRAM
     84  3845
     85  3845							; Function copies a RAM prototype ROM bank into the destination RAM bank.  Typically
     86  3845							; the variable definitions are in the ROM shadow because this allows auto-initialisation
     87  3845							; of the variable contents from ROM declarations, but still allows access to them as
     88  3845							; variables when the correct RAM bank is switched in.	Code is also, of course, copied
     89  3845							; into the RAM destination so that code is callable whenever the ROM *or* RAM bank is
     90  3845							; switched in.  Further, if multiple copies are made to multiple RAM banks, then the
     91  3845							; code co-lives in all banks and may run even as bankswitching occurs between those
     92  3845							; banks -- by the very code itself.
     93  3845
     94  3845							; Note: Relies on ROM_Bank having being set via CALL mechanism to call this function
     95  3845		       85 bb		      sta	Board_AddressR+1
     96  3847		       86 da		      stx	O_ROM_Source_Bank	; source bank
     97  3849		       84 bf		      sty	RAM_Bank	; destination bank
     98  384b
     99  384b		       a0 00		      ldy	#0
    100  384d		       84 ba		      sty	Board_AddressR
    101  384f		       84 bc		      sty	Board_AddressW
    102  3851		       a9 14		      lda	#>($1000+RAM_WRITE)
    103  3853		       85 bd		      sta	Board_AddressW+1
    104  3855
    105  3855							; Iterate 4 pages (1K) for complete bank copy
    106  3855
    107  3855		       a9 04		      lda	#4
    108  3857		       85 d9		      sta	O_CopyCount
    109  3859
    110  3859		       84 db	   CopyPage   sty	O_Index
    111  385b		       a5 da		      lda	O_ROM_Source_Bank
    112  385d		       20 32 f8 	      jsr	GetROMByte	; get byte from ROM shadow bank
    113  3860							;tax
    114  3860		       a4 db		      ldy	O_Index
    115  3862		       a6 bf		      ldx	RAM_Bank
    116  3864		       20 40 f8 	      jsr	PutBoardCharacter	;6+21(A)	 write byte to RAM bank
    117  3867
    118  3867		       a4 db		      ldy	O_Index
    119  3869		       c8		      iny
    120  386a		       d0 ed		      bne	CopyPage
    121  386c
    122  386c		       e6 bb		      inc	Board_AddressR+1
    123  386e		       e6 bd		      inc	Board_AddressW+1
    124  3870
    125  3870		       c6 d9		      dec	O_CopyCount
    126  3872		       d0 e5		      bne	CopyPage
    127  3874
    128  3874		       a4 bf		      ldy	RAM_Bank	; TODO: remove!?
    129  3876		       60		      rts
    130  3877

    441  397c							; IF the creature runs out of time to do stuff, then rts HOWEVER the creature must eventually do something
    442  397c							;  as it will be continually called in available time-slices until it does. This can lockup the system.

    194  78ba							; Now process the blank stack.  This stack holds all the recently blanked squares
    195  78ba							; and determines (and moves) BOXs or diamonds into these squares.  The space vacated
    196  78ba							; by these objects are added again to the blank stack.

    202  78bd
      0  78bd					      DEFINE_SUBROUTINE	SwitchObjects	;=72
      1  78bd		       00 0f	   BANK_SwitchObjects =	_CURRENT_BANK
      2  78bd					      SUBROUTINE
      3  78bd				   SwitchObjects
    204  78bd							; TJ: used by:
    205  78bd							; - BANK_FIXED.asm
    206  78bd
    207  78bd							; The game loop has come to an end. The only possible "still happening" thing is the sort, which runs
    208  78bd							; in parallel with other processes (objects, draw stack, etc). We may or may not want to wait for the
    209  78bd							; sort to complete.  This code does all the checks needed to switch to the next game frame.
    210  78bd
    211  78bd		       ad 84 02 	      lda	INTIM	; 4
    212  78c0		       c9 03		      cmp	#SEGTIME_SWITCHOBJECTS	; 2
    213  78c2		       90 f8		      bcc	EarlyAbort	; 2/3= 8
      0  78c4					      STRESS_TIME	SEGTIME_SWITCHOBJECTS
      1  78c4				  -	      IF	TEST_SEGTIME_SWITCHOBJECTS = 1
      2  78c4				  -
      3  78c4				  -
      4  78c4				  -
      5  78c4				  -
      6  78c4				  -
      7  78c4				  -	      echo	"***** WARNING! STRESS_TIME enabled @", ., "! *****"
      8  78c4				  -	      bne	. - 7
      9  78c4					      ENDIF
    215  78c4
    216  78c4							; If we're undertime, then abort. The sort will continue to run, and that's great. Only when
    217  78c4							; we're at the throttle cutoff do we switch game-frames.
    218  78c4
    219  78c4							;sec
    220  78c4		       a5 ae		      lda	Throttle	;3
    221  78c6		       e9 a0		      sbc	#MAX_THROTTLE	;2
    222  78c8		       90 f2		      bcc	EarlyAbort	;2/3		 plenty of time left!
    223  78ca
    224  78ca							; Time is up. But we may be in a level which requires perfect sorting
    225  78ca							; So we check for these levels, and wait for the sort to complete for those.
    226  78ca
    227  78ca		       24 ad		      bit	levelDisplay	;3
    228  78cc		       50 08		      bvc	keepFractional	;2/3		 screen does not require complete sort
    229  78ce
    230  78ce							; We have a level which requires the sort to go to completion
    231  78ce							; Check to see if the sort is finished...
    232  78ce
    233  78ce		       a4 cf		      ldy	sortPtr	;3
    234  78d0		       d0 ea		      bne	EarlyAbort	;2/3		 sort still in progress, so wait
    235  78d2		       a4 ce		      ldy	sortRequired	;3
    236  78d4		       10 e6		      bpl	EarlyAbort	;2/3		 sort still in progress, so wait
    237  78d6
    238  78d6		       85 ae	   keepFractional sta	Throttle	;3		 save fractional 'left over' bit
    239  78d8
    240  78d8							; Pause the game with B/W switch:
    241  78d8
    242  78d8		       a5 80		      lda	gameMode
    243  78da							;		  ora LookingAround		  ; New behavour of looking around pauses creatures when activated.
    244  78da		       30 14		      bmi	.paused	; pause flag set
    245  78dc
    246  78dc							; Now that we have completed processing the object stack, we switch
    247  78dc							; the stack bank pointers for the next time around.
    248  78dc
    249  78dc		       a5 85		      lda	ObjStackNum	;3
    250  78de		       49 01		      eor	#1	;2
    251  78e0		       aa		      tax		;2
    252  78e1		       86 85		      stx	ObjStackNum	;3		 swap stacks @here
    253  78e3
    254  78e3							; STOP the sort so it doesn't corrupt the "other" object stack. Sort may get a look-in immediately after
    255  78e3							; this code is finished, so we don't want it to do something unexpected!
    256  78e3
    257  78e3		       a0 ff		      ldy	#<(-1)	;2
    258  78e5		       84 ce		      sty	sortRequired	;3
    259  78e7		       c8		      iny		;2		 Y==0
    260  78e8		       84 cf		      sty	sortPtr	;3
    261  78ea
    262  78ea							; Initialise the iterator and stack pointer for next time around.
    263  78ea							; Previously the stack pointer auto-initialised by popping the stack. Now we have an iterator it's
    264  78ea							; necessary to initialise both.
    265  78ea
    266  78ea		       84 d7		      sty	ObjIterator	;3		 Y==0
    267  78ec		       94 86		      sty	ObjStackPtr,x	;4
    268  78ee
    269  78ee		       84 89		      sty	ScreenDrawPhase	;3
    270  78f0				   .paused
    271  78f0		       60	   quickExit  rts		;6
    272  78f1

    379  7961
    380  7961							; Nice addition limits overflow of the stack, BUT always reserves a spot for the man.
    381  7961							; Objects are unceremoniously dumped when there's not enough space.  This is just trying to cater
    382  7961							; for a no-win situation. Try and preserve the player at the cost of correct gameplay. Avoid crashing.
    383  7961
    384  7961
    385  7961				  -	      IF	TYPE_MAN != 0
    386  7961				  -	      cmp	#TYPE_MAN	; 2
    387  7961					      ENDIF
    388  7961		       f0 04		      beq	alwaysAllowMan	; 2/3
    389  7963
    390  7963		       c0 7e		      cpy	#OBJ_STACK_SIZE-2	; 2	     reserve 1 last-gasp slot for man only
    391  7965		       b0 06		      bcs	insertDone	; 2/3= 6    no room -- drop object
    392  7967				   alwaysAllowMan

      3  7a06				   TimeSlice
    559  7a06
    560  7a06							; FIRST check the time is sufficient for the smallest of the timeslices. Not much point
    561  7a06							; going ahead if there's insufficient time. This allows the previous character drawing to
    562  7a06							; be much smaller in time, as they don't have to include the timeslice code overhead.
    563  7a06
    564  7a06		       ad 84 02 	      lda	INTIM	; 4
    565  7a09		       c9 05		      cmp	#SEGTIME_MINIMUM_TIMESLICE	; 2
    566  7a0b		       90 de		      bcc	timeExit	; 2(3)
    567  7a0d
    568  7a0d							; Uses the phase variable to vector to the correct processing code for the given timeslice
    569  7a0d							; Code may be in any bank. Avoid the fixed bank at all costs!	Once a section is complete
    570  7a0d							; it should increment ScreenDrawPhase.
    571  7a0d
    572  7a0d							; Switched-in bank(s) are undefined after this function is called!
    573  7a0d
    574  7a0d		       a9 06		      lda	#BANK_TS_PhaseVectorLO	; 2
    575  7a0f		       85 3f		      sta	SET_BANK	; 3
    576  7a11
    577  7a11		       a6 89		      ldx	ScreenDrawPhase	; 3		 current phase of drawing
    578  7a13		       bd 11 f5 	      lda	TS_PhaseVectorLO,x	; 4
    579  7a16		       85 d9		      sta	TS_Vector	; 3
    580  7a18		       bd 16 f5 	      lda	TS_PhaseVectorHI,x	; 4
    581  7a1b		       85 da		      sta	TS_Vector+1	; 3
    582  7a1d
    583  7a1d		       bd 1b f5 	      lda	TS_PhaseBank,x	; 4
    584  7a20		       85 3f		      sta	SET_BANK	; 3		 switch bank
    585  7a22
    586  7a22		       6c d9 00 	      jmp	(TS_Vector)	; 3 = 40	 vector to timeslice handler

    806  7afc				   NewFrameBD
    807  7afc							; the (at least) 220 cycles wasted in the above... bugs me!
    808  7afc							; the below is an unrolled version.  I've moved some other code between the sync writes, effectively saving um... 22 cycles/frame.
    809  7afc							; This required TIM64T values to be increased by 1 for each platform (we have actually gained back some usable time :)
    810  7afc
    811  7afc							;bit NextLevelTrigger
    812  7afc							;bpl NextCaveLevel		  ; game-triggered next level
    813  7afc							;bvs RestartCaveNextPlayer	  ; loss of life
    814  7afc
    815  7afc							; Note: VSYNC must NOT be on when starting a new cave! Else you get annoying TV signals.
    816  7afc
    817  7afc		       a9 0e		      lda	#%1110	; VSYNC ON
    818  7afe		       85 42	   .loopVSync sta	WSYNC
    819  7b00		       85 40		      sta	VSYNC
    820  7b02		       4a		      lsr
    821  7b03		       d0 f9		      bne	.loopVSync	; branch until VYSNC has been reset
    822  7b05
    823  7b05							; moved *after* the loop since this allows to *increase* timer values by 1!

    847  7b1e							; A 42-cycle timing window in the screen draw code.  Perform any general
    848  7b1e							; per-frame code here, provided it takes exactly 42 cycles to execute.
    849  7b1e							; TJ: Well, not exactly 42 cycles, but it works! :)

      2  7b20

   1088  7bdf							; This manages character animation on a per-object basis.  Morph/animate these
